Jamison Brereton

61 (773)
Soma Pavama╠Дna
Amah─лyu ─Ас╣Еgirasa
30 verses: g─Бyatr─л, arranged in trcas ╠е
The first sixty hymns of the Soma Maс╣Зс╕Нala, all in g─Бyatr─л meter, are arranged in the normal order of descending number of verses, starting with hymns of ten verses and ending with those of four. (The only exception is the ─Аpr─л hymn, IX.5, which has eleven.) But the g─Бyatr─л sequence ends with six thirty-verse hymns (IX.61тАУ66), followed by one with thirty-two verses (IX.67)тАФall arranged in tr╠еcas (the final two verses in IX.67 are supplements) and each attributed to a different poet or group of poetsтАФbefore the jagat─л group begins. It is probably not an accident that these groupings of tr╠еcas come at the end of the g─Бyatr─л sequence, since, as agglomerations of three-verse sequences, they logically follow the four-verse hymns.
In this particular hymn there is little evidence of unity either within tr╠еcas or between them: the standard topics of soma hymnsтАФthe details of preparation (e.g., vss. 4тАУ5) and the gods for whom heтАЩs prepared (e.g., vss. 8тАУ9), the cosmic connections of Soma (e.g., vss. 10, 16, 18), and the largesse and aid we ask him for (e.g., vss. 3, 23тАУ24)тАФ
are strung together in no apparent order. There is a discernible tendency, however, to emphasize SomaтАЩs role in combating hostile forces, either directly or by strengthening someone else to do so, especially Indra. The hymn begins with two verses mention ing some of IndraтАЩs exploits performed under the influence of Soma, though without

naming Indra, and the theme of Soma the smiter and aggressive warrior returns toward the end of the hymn and dominates the last two tr╠еcas (vss. 19тАУ20, 22, 24тАУ30).

Jamison Brereton Notes

61-67 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

On the place of these long hymns in the structure of the maс╣Зс╕Нala, see published introduction. to IX.61. All of these hymns consist of collections of tс╣Ыcas of varying degrees of cohesion. In fact, it is surprising how few tс╣Ыcas display a real attempt at thematic or lexical unity, and what they do show is often simply the byproduct of the fact that both the lexicon and thematic preoccupations of Maс╣Зс╕Нala IX are comparatively limited and so similar words and themes are not unlikely to show up in adjacent verses. This lack of unity contrasts, I think (this is my unsystematic and anecdotal impression) with collections of tс╣Ыcas in other maс╣Зс╕Нalas, notably VIII.

English translation:

тАЬFlow, Indu, for (Indra’s) food with that (juice) of yours which in battles overthrow ninety and nine (cities of the foe).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Ay─Б v─лt─л may also mean ‘with that food’

Jamison Brereton

Flow around in pursuit (of him) who amid your raptures, o drop, smashed down the nine and ninetyтАФ

Jamison Brereton Notes

The published translation fails to render the demon. ay─Б╠Бthat opens the hymn; more literal would be тАЬflow around in this pursuit (of him) тАжтАЭ Geldner (n. 1) considers ay─Б╠Бa kind of attraction from

*asya тАШof himтАЩ, the missing antecedent to y├бс╕е in b, but the prominent position of ay─Б╠Бshould be registered. Presumably ay─Б╠Бv─лt─л╠Бis gesturing towards the physical ritual activity happening right now.

The unnamed referent in the rel. cl. of bc is of course Indra; the тАЬnine and ninetyтАЭ are fortresses / strongholds, as in IV.26.3 тАж p├║raс╕е тАж n├бva s─Бk├бс╣Г navat─л╠Бс╕е ┼Ы├бmbarasya. This referent is postponed to the 2nd vs.: p├║raс╕е opens vs. 2.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This tс╣Ыca shows some signs of unity. The 1st two vss. are a syntactic unit, with the objects of the verb in 1c partly postponed to 2ab. The third vs. has as its verb p├бri тАж kс╣г├бr─Б, which echoes p├бri srava in 1a.

and as for that Turva┼Ыa and Yadu… .

Jamison Brereton Notes

As was just noted, p├║raс╕е completes the acc. phrase navat─л╠Бr n├бva that serves as obj.

to av─Б╠Бhan in 1c, as the parallel IV.26.3 just cited demonstrates. But av─Б╠Бhan has another object in vs. 2, namely ┼Ы├бmbaram in b, as shown by a different passage in the Indra cycle of Maс╣Зс╕Нala IV, IV.30.14 ├бv─Бhann indra ┼Ы├бmbaram.

The third p─Бda of this vs. is radically incomplete, consisting only of a particle, a demon., and two acc. PNs: ├бdha ty├бс╣Г turv├б┼Ыam y├бdum. On purely structural grounds, it would make sense to make these parallel to ┼Ы├бmbaram in b, as objects of av─Б╠Бhan (in 1c).

However, this structural argument runs into problems of mythological content. Although Turva┼Ыa and Yadu are sometimes enemies of Indra (see, e.g., VII.19.2), at other times they are under IndraтАЩs protection. In particular, in the Indra cycle from which IV.26.3 and IV.30.14, the parallels to our vss. 1-2ab, were cited above, T + Y are rescued by Indra: IV.30.17 ut├б ty─Б╠Бturv├б┼Ы─Бy├бd┼л, тАж / ├нndraс╕е тАж ap─Бrayat тАЬAnd Indra brought these two, T + Y, to the far shore,тАЭ just three vss. later than the smiting of ┼Ъambara. Note further that IV.30.17a is very like our p─Бda, a dimeter line with an introduction. disyllabic connective, a form of the demonstr. sy├б- / ty├б-, and the two names, though with a dual dvandva turv├б┼Ы─Бy├бd┼л rather than two individual acc. sgs. On this basis, IтАЩm afraid the simple solution of taking T + Y as further victims of Indra should be abandoned, in favor of supplying (or at least assuming) a positive verb to govern them, such as GeldnerтАЩs (n. 2c) тАЬerretteteтАЭ or RenouтАЩs тАЬsauva.тАЭ

English translation:

тАЬIndu, conqueror of horses, shower forth horses with cattle and gold and unbounded food.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Stream around to us horseflesh, as horse-finder, and (wealth) in cattle and gold, o drop,
and thousandfold refreshments.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The Inhaltsakk. with p├бri тАж kс╣г├бr─Б are disharmonious in formation, with the sg.

noun ├б┼Ыvam (rendered in the published translation as the mass noun тАШhorsefleshтАЩ, perhaps a bit too vividly) in p─Бda a followed by two possessive adj. g├│mat and h├нraс╣Зyavat тАШpossessing / consisting of cattle (and) goldтАЩ in p─Бda b, followed by a pl. NP sahasr├нс╣З─лr ├нс╣гaс╕е тАШthousandfold refreshmentsтАЩ in c. In a we might have expected ├б┼Ыv─Бvat тАШpossessing / consisting of horsesтАЩ, to match the adjectival forms in b, but the phonologically similar and adjacent a┼Ыvav├нd тАШhorse-findingтАЩ may have blocked it (to avoid *├б┼Ыv─Бvad a┼Ыvav├нd [though some RVic poets would have loved that phrase]).

Jamison Brereton Notes

This tс╣Ыca shows some signs of unity. The 1st two vss. are a syntactic unit, with the objects of the verb in 1c partly postponed to 2ab. The third vs. has as its verb p├бri тАж kс╣г├бr─Б, which echoes p├бri srava in 1a.

English translation:

тАЬWe solicit your friendship as you drop flowing over the filter.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

While you are purifying yourself, while you are flooding the filter, we choose your companionship.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Both Geldner and Renou render p├бvam─Бnasya as simply the epithet Pavam─Бna, but this loses the parallelism between the two gen. sg. pres. participles that open and close the hemistich: p├бvam─Бnasya тАж abhyundat├бс╕е. I render these participles as тАЬwhileтАЭ clauses, to avoid the awkward тАЬwe choose the companionship of you who are Xing.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

There are faint signs of unity in this tс╣Ыca: the word pav├нtram тАШfilterтАЩ is found in vss. 4 and 5, and both 4 and 6 have pres. mid. participles derived from тИЪp┼л тАШpurifyтАЩ (p├бvam─Бna- 4a, pun─Бn├б- 6a), but since this is a Soma Pavam─Бna hymn, this is hardly remarkable.

English translation:

тАЬThe birth of your juice is on high; the earth has received (your) intense happiness and abundant food, though (these) exist (naturally) in heaven.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yajus. 26.16; though these exist naturally inheaven: api ca dyuloke vidyam─Бnam svatas: bh┼лmy─Б = bh┼лmiс╕е + ─Б (with the lision of the visarga in the saс╣Гhit─Б text)

Jamison Brereton

It was born high above from your stalk; though it was in heaven, on earth it took for itself
mighty shelter and great fame.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The topic of the verse seems to be heavenly versus earthly soma. See L├╝ders 204.

On j─Бt├бm as an adj., rather than (with Geldner, Renou, L├╝ders 204, Ober II.16) the noun тАШbirthтАЩ, see comm. ad IX.55.2. Another arg. for taking it as adjectival here is that the same form is clearly an adj. in 13a. As in IX.55.2, I take the missing referent to be тАШhoneyтАЩ (m├бdhu) on the basis of IX.18.2.

P─Бda b contains several forms requiring disc., esp. what appears in the Saс╣Гhit─Б text as bh┼л╠Бmy. This is analyzed, irregularly, by the Pp as bh┼л╠Бmiс╕е. Grassmann gives the form as bh┼л╠Бm─л but identifies it as a nom. sg. to bh┼л╠Бmi-. Oldenberg refers to the considerable lit. on the form, opting for a loc. interpr. (as do all the standard tr.). Wackernagel has a curiously split opinion: in AiG I.337 (1896) he identifies it as a loc., while in AiG III.136-37 (1930) he decides instead for the nom., though referring to his former opinion - and in the same vol. (III.155) he says the same form doesnтАЩt have to be a loc. (тАЬтАж muss nicht notwendig as Lok. bh┼л╠Бm─л gefasst werdenтАЭ), but could alternatively be either a nom. bh┼л╠Бm─л or an instr. bh┼л╠Бmy─Б. The context, with the contrast div├н с╣г├бt тАЬthough being in heavenтАЭ with loc. div├н, certainly favors a loc. interpr. for the form, even though taking тАШearthтАЩ as the subject of the clause is possible: тАЬearth took it, though it was in heaven.тАЭ In sum, I think the loc. interpr. is most likely, with an -─л (or -i) loc, to a fem. i-stem, like v├йd─л (or v├йdi) in II.3.4 (see comm. ad loc.). A bh┼л╠Бmi with short final vowel is metrically better here (as v├йdi is in II.3.4), but it may result from shortening in hiatus.

The neut. part. s├бt has, in my opinion, the concessive value often found with the pres.

part. to тИЪas, though most tr. donтАЩt render it as such (and Renou rejects this interpr.). It modifies the unexpressed m├бdhu in my view, but the neut. ├бndhas- acdg. to most others.

─Б╠Бdade is another ambig. form.: it can be either a 1st or a 3rd sg. mid. pf. (or a 1st sg.

mid. pres.). Grassmann takes it as a 1st sg. pf., as does Geldner (тАЬDen im Himmel befindlichen (Trank) nehme ich auf der Erde zu michтАЭ), but a 3rd sg., with the soma (represented by m├бdhu or ├бndhaс╕е) as subject (with Renou, L├╝ders, Ober) allows p─Бda c to serve as obj. of ─Б╠Бdade - Geldner has to take it as an independent nominal clause - and the Grassmann/Geldner interpr. also introduces a 1st sg.

that has no other place in the context, where the 1st pl. reigns.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe pure (Soma) has genitive rated in heaven the great Vai┼Ыv─Бnara light like the wonderful thunder.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Vai┼Ыv─Бnara light: i.e., Agni, the son of Vai┼Ыv─Бnara

Jamison Brereton

Purifying himself he has begotten thunder dazzling like that of heaven and the lofty light belonging to all men.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The question in this vs. is how to interpr. the simile in p─Бda b, div├б┼Ы citr├бс╣Г n├б tanyat├║m. It has been variously rendered. Note first that in none of the available interpr.

(that I know of) is the simile particle n├б positioned in the expected 2nd position, so that conforming to the usual structure of the simile cannot be used as a criterion to decide which interpr. is correct. We have had occasion to note this issue before in Maс╣Зс╕Нala IX; see disc.

ad IX.57.3. Renou takes the whole of b as a simile, with the тАЬthunderтАЭ matching тАЬlightтАЭ (c) in the frame; in addition he supplies a different subject for the simile: тАЬPavam─Бna a engendr├й la haute lumi├иre propre ├а (Agni) Vai┼Ыv─Бnara, / comme (les dieux ont engendr├й) le tonnerre ├йclatante du ciel.тАЭ This is not impossible, of course, but introducing the gods seems unnecessary, and are they the usual creators of thunder anyway? L├╝dersтАЩs (266) interpr. is similar, though he allows Pavam─Бna as subj. of both the simile and the frame. I find GeldnerтАЩs interpr. more appealing: he considers tanyat├║m part of the frame, with the simile restricted to div├б┼Ы citr├бm. тАЬSich l├дuternd hat er den Donner, grell wie den des Himmels, hervorgebracht.тАЭ The c p─Бda provides a parallel object, rather than constituting the frame as in the Renou/L├╝ders interpr. My tr. essentially follows Geldner The тАЬthunderтАЭ that Soma engendered is the noise produced by the pressing, esp. by the pressing stones, which is constantly remarked on. It is comparable to the thunder of heaven. All interpr. must silently reckon with the synaesthesia introduced by the point of the comparison in the simile, citr├б- тАШbright, brilliant, glittering, dazzlingтАЩ, an adj. that ordinarily characterizes visual phenomena not auditory ones (though itтАЩs a not uncommon transfer; cf. Engl. тАЬbrilliant tone,тАЭ etc., used of voices and musical instruments). For a similar ex. cf. VI.6.2 ┼Ыvit─Бnas tanyat├║с╕е тАЬbrightening thunder.тАЭ This synaesthetic comparison provides a lead-in to the second object, the тАЬlight belonging to all men.тАЭ Both Geldner and Renou take jy├│tir vai┼Ыv─Бnar├бm as referring to Agni Vai┼Ыv─Бnara specifically.

This is certainly possible, though it is not the soma pressing that ordinarily kindles the ritual fire. I prefer to take it more generally as shared light, perhaps localized as the sun, which would continue the heavenly theme of p─Бda b. Alternatively, this p─Бda, which is entirely in the neuter, may be nominative not accusative and refer to Soma himself. This interpr. may be favored by the matching p─Бda at the end of the tс╣Ыca, 18c jy├│tir v├н┼Ыvam sv├аr dс╣Ы┼Ы├й тАЬ(as) light for everyone to see the sun,тАЭ where the soma sapтАФthat is, soma itselfтАФis identified as this light. I would therefore suggest an alternative tr. of p─Бda c here: тАЬ(he) the lofty light belonging to all men.тАЭ

Note also the two forms of r├бsa- тАШsapтАЩ in 17a and 18a (the two p─Бdas are scramblings of each other: 17a p├бvam─Бnasya te r├бsaс╕е, 18a p├бvam─Бna r├бsas t├бva, with different case forms of p├бvam─Бna- and enclitic versus full form of the gen. sg. 2nd ps. prn.). Jamison Brereton Notes

I am, reluctantly, taking d├бkс╣гa- as an adj. here (as in IX.62.4), with Geldner and Renou, though it is generally a masc. noun. Alternatively a noun interpr. is possible (cf. Ober I.457 тАЬdein Saft ist F├дhigkeitтАЭ): тАЬyour sap shines forth brilliant as skillтАЭ or тАЬтАж shines as brilliant skill,тАЭ though I still prefer the adjectival interpr. See RenouтАЩs disc.

Scarlatta (237) takes v├н r─Бjati as тАШrulesтАЩ (тАЬdein Saft herrscht weithin als K├╢nig тАжтАЭ A pun is certainly possible here, but the insistent light imagery (dyum─Б╠Бn in b and the whole c p─Бda) suggests that the тАШshineтАЩ sense is the dominant one.

In c Geldner takes v├н┼Ыvam as the modifier of jy├│tiс╕е (тАЬтАж ist alles lichtтАЭ); so also Scarlatta (237).

This is certainly possible, and jy├│tir vai┼Ыv─Бnar├бm in 16c might support it. But тАЬfor everyone / all to see the sunтАЭ is a locution encountered elsewhere (I.15.1, 5, VIII.49.8, X.136.1), incl.

nearby IX.48.4. My interpr. is shared with Renou and Ober (I.457).

Note also the two forms of r├бsa- тАШsapтАЩ in 17a and 18a (the two p─Бdas are scramblings of each other: 17a p├бvam─Бnasya te r├бsaс╕е, 18a p├бvam─Бna r├бsas t├бva, with different case forms of p├бvam─Бna- and enclitic versus full form of the gen. sg. 2nd ps. prn.). English translation:

тАЬFlow you who did help Indra to slay Vс╣Ыtra, who obstructed the great waters.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Purify yourself, you who helped Indra to smash Vr╠еtra,
who was obstructing the great waters.

Jamison Brereton Notes

A nice example where surface grammar clashes with mythological content and the latter wins. P─Бda b, the complex object of ─Б╠Бvitha тАШyou helpedтАЩ in a, consists of an infinitival phrase with the obj. of the inf. тАЬattractedтАЭ into the dative, while its subject remains acc.: ├нndraс╣Г vс╣Ыtr─Б╠Бya h├бntave тАЬyou helped Indra to smite Vс╣Ыtra.тАЭ But c, a further specification of this obj., contains an acc. sg. masc. participial phrase vavriv─Б╠Бс╣Гsam mah─л╠Бr ap├бс╕е тАЬobstructing the great waters.тАЭ On the surface, the only noun this can modify is ├нndram because this is the only available acc. sg. masc., but of course it is Vс╣Ыtra who obstructed the waters. Though vс╣Ыtr─Б╠Бya appears in the dative, it must be the referent of the acc. participle - thus suggesting that тАЬattractionтАЭ in infinitival phrases is a very late and superficial phenomenon. Unless with Renou we want simply to denominate it a тАЬformule morphologiquement non adapt├йe au contexte.тАЭ I prefer to think that the poet enjoyed producing the syntactic misdirection.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda a consists of the etymologically identical phrases tv├│t─Бsaс╕е тАШaided by youтАЩ and t├бv─Б╠Бvas─Б тАШwith your helpтАЩ, both containing forms of the 2nd sg. prn. and nominal forms of тИЪav тАШhelp, aidтАЩ.

P─Бda b contains a curious verbal periphrasis, sy─Б╠Бma vanv├бntaс╕е тАЬmay we be combatting,тАЭ with opt. to тИЪas as aux. plus the pres. act, part. to van├│ti. This expression does not seem to be conveying anything different from the opt. to the same pres. stem, vanuy─Б╠Бma (5x), e.g., X.38.3 tv├бy─Б vay├бс╣Г t─Б╠Бn [┼Ы├бtr┼лn] vanuy─Бma тАЬWith you might we combat those (rivals).тАЭ As noted above, vrat├б- in this p─Бda may have been chosen to recall vс╣Ыtr├бphonologically, forming a faint ring with the тИЪvс╣Ы forms in 22 vс╣Ыtr─Б╠Бya тАж vavriv─Б╠Бс╣Гsam. It may even be that j─Бgс╣Ыhi тАШbe watchfulтАЩ evokes a form of тИЪhan, as in 20a j├бghnir vс╣Ыtr├бm; see also jah─л╠Бin 26b.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬA hundred foes harm you not, purposing to give wealth when being purified you are benevolently inclined.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Purposing to give wealth: makhasyase = asmabhy─Бm dhanam d─Бtum icchasi; cf. RV 9.020.07, where makhaс╕е = d─Бnam; RV. 9.064.026, where makhasyuvam = dhanak─Бmam; RV. 9. 101.5, makhasyate = stutibhiс╕е p┼лj─Бm icchati; thus makhaс╕е = yaj├▒am or dhanam or d─Бnam; from magh = great

Jamison Brereton

A hundred crooks [/wool tufts] will never confound you when you are eager to give largesse,
when you, becoming purified, do battle [/act bounteously].

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. is rather cleverer than the two that precede it. In p─Бda a the nom. pl. root noun hr├║taс╕е is, in my opinion, a pun. It belongs to the root тИЪhvс╣Ы тАШgo crookedly, curveтАЩ, and its sense was disc., e.g., by Hoffmann (Fs. Thieme [1980] =Aufs. III.753-54). He suggests that here it refers to unevennesses (Unebenheiten) in the fleece sieve (i.e., as I see it, the curvy tufts of wool), just as, in the other occurrence of this root noun (VI.4.5), it refers to the curves of a race course (see comm. ad loc.). The literal sense here then is that though the soma must navigate around the tufts on the sieve, they will not keep it from completing the course. The second sense is one referring to unscrupulous enemiesтАФEngl. тАШcrookтАЩ is an exact semantic matchтАФand the point is that when Soma wishes to dispense goods to us, our crooked enemies canтАЩt divert him.

The word family that includes makh├б- and the denom. makhasy├б- found here displays both тАШcombatтАЩ and тАШgenerosityтАЩ senses; see comm. ad I.18.9 and, for the verb, III.31.7. Here I think both are at play, and this double sense is encouraged by the context: as noted, this tс╣Ыca focuses on combatting enemies, and the first hemistich of this vs. states that these enemies cannot stop Soma. But the tс╣Ыca also concerns SomaтАЩs giving, esp. in the last two vss.: 26a тАЬbring wealth … 26c тАЬgiveтАЭ тАж 27b тАЬeager to give largesse.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

This tс╣Ыca focuses even more strongly on combat, with forms of тИЪhan in 25 and 26 and тАШdo battleтАЩ (makhasy├б-) in 27. Generosity is also a topic.

Griffith

A hundred obstacles have ne’er checked
thee when fain to give thy boons,
When, being cleansed, thou combatest.

тАЬ(Enjoying) the friendship of you here and you excellent food, Indu, may we overcome our assailants.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Food: dyumnam dyotate’rya┼Ыo v─Бnnam v─Б (Nirukta. 5.5)

In the companionship of you here, in your highest brilliance, o drop, might we overcome those who do battle.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first two p─Бdas open with somewhat emphatic 2nd sg. genitives, the first with a fronted initially accented demonst. + enclitic (├бsya te), the second with a more conventional full form of the prn. (t├бva). See disc. ad IX.66.14.

English translation:

тАЬWith your weapons which are formidable and sharp for slaying (the foe), defend us from the scorn (of our enemies).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Your fearful sharp weapons, which exist to injure,
(with them) guard us from the insult of anyone at all.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The nominal rel. cl. in ab has no resumptive prn. in the main cl. of c, though тАЬwith these/themтАЭ is clearly the intent.

On the construction of dh┼л╠Бrvane here, see Keydana, Infin. 247, though the arbitrary line he tends to draw between тАЬtrueтАЭ infinitives and datival purpose nouns seems over-strict here.

As is shown by IX.29.5 r├бkс╣гa … svan─Б╠Бt samasya k├бsya cit (cited by Geldner), nid├бс╕е must be an abl. (as we would expect in any case with a form of тИЪrakс╣г) with a dependent gen., the indefinite samasya.
